    <script type="text/javascript" nonce="0267fcce6d4a49d89121ac2420a22a85">

        function getParameter(parameterName) {
            let result = null,
                tmp = [];
            location.search
                .substr(1)
                .split("&")
                .forEach(function (item) {
                    tmp = item.split("=");
                    if (tmp[0] === parameterName) result = tmp[1];
                });
            return result;
        }

        var SeamlessAccessService = {
            spUrl: "/action/ssostart",
            returnURL: window.location.href,
            my_context: 'seamlessaccess.org',
            queryParamsDelimiter: encodeURIComponent('?'),

            getWAYFLessUrl: function (entityId) {
                let redirectURL = getParameter('redirectUri');
                if(redirectURL == null){
                    redirectURL = encodeURIComponent(this.returnURL);
                }
                if(redirectURL.indexOf('saml_referrer') < 0){
                    redirectURL += encodeURIComponent(((redirectURL.indexOf(this.queryParamsDelimiter) !== -1) ? '&' : '?') + 'saml_referrer');
                }
                return this.spUrl + "?idp=" + encodeURIComponent(entityId)
                    + "&redirectUri=" + redirectURL;
            },
            retrieveEntity: function () {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.entities(self.my_context)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // get the results
                            var results = res.data;
                            return resolve(results);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            reject('retrieve entity error: ' + err);
                        });
                });
            },
            updateEntity: function (entitydata) {
                var self = this;
                var ps = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                var jsonObj = {};
                try {
                    //try to parse it, if it is a json string
                    jsonObj = JSON.parse(entitydata.val());
                } catch (e) {
                    jsonObj = entitydata;
                }
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    ps.update(self.my_context, jsonObj)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            // Process the results
                            var ssoInstitutions = res.data;
                            return resolve(ssoInstitutions);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to update the local storage duo to: ' + err);
                            reject(err);
                        });
                })
            },
            removeEntity: function (entityId) {
                var self = this;
                var persistService = new thiss.PersistenceService('https://service.seamlessaccess.org/ps/');

                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    persistService.remove(self.my_context, entityId)
                        .then(function (res) {
                            return resolve(res);
                        }, function (err) {
                            // failed
                            console.log('failed to remove from local storage duo to: ' + err);
                        });
                })
            },
            getAccessibleEntityStatus: function (doi, entityId, entityTitle) {
                return new Promise(function (resolve) {
                    $.ajax({
                        type: 'POST',
                        url: '/action/seamlessAccess',
                        accept: {
                            text: "application/json"
                        },
                        data: {doi: doi, entityid: entityId, entityTitle: entityTitle, eventGroupKey: 'fa640ba9-776f-43cd-ab3a-0e1ab16f89e4'}

                    }).done(function (status) {
                        return resolve(status);
                    });
                });
            },
            getEntitiesWithAllInfo: function (doi) {
                let self = this,
                    arrayOfPromises = [];
                return new Promise(function (resolve, reject) {
                    self.retrieveEntity().then(function (res) {
                        let allSsoInstitutions = res;
                        for (let i in allSsoInstitutions) {
                            let ssoInstitution = allSsoInstitutions[i];
                            arrayOfPromises.push(new Promise(function (resolve) {
                                self.getAccessibleEntityStatus(doi, ssoInstitution.entity.entityID, ssoInstitution.entity.title)
                                    .then(function (entityStatus) {
                                        resolve({
                                            entityID: ssoInstitution.entity.entityID,
                                            entityTitle: ssoInstitution.entity.title,
                                            entityStatusObj: entityStatus,
                                            entitySsoUrl: self.getWAYFLessUrl(ssoInstitution.entity.entityID)
                                        });
                                    }, function (err) {
                                        console.log('failed to get the entity status: ' + err);
                                    });
                            }));
                        }
                        Promise.all(arrayOfPromises)
                            .then(function (finalResponse) {
                                resolve(finalResponse);
                            });

                    }).catch(function (err) {
                        reject(err);
                    })
                });
            }
        };

        window.addEventListener('load', function () {
            document.querySelectorAll(".sso-institution").forEach(function (institution) {
                var entityId = institution.getAttribute('data-entityid');
                var entityName = institution.getAttribute('data-name');
                var entitydata = {
                    entityID: entityId,
                    title: entityName
                };
                institution.addEventListener("click", function (e) {
                    e.preventDefault();
                    var self = this;
                    SeamlessAccessService.updateEntity(entitydata).then(function (res) {
                        console.log(res);
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    }).catch(function (err){
                        window.location.href = self.href;
                    });
                });
            });
        });

                     <p>College of Sciences and Institute for Sustainable Energy, Shanghai University, Shanghai, 200444 China</p><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/Zhao/Shengyu">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span><span class="accordion-tabbed__tab-mobile  accordion__closed"><a href="/authored-by/Li/Caixia" class="author-name accordion-tabbed__control" data-id="a7" data-db-target-for="a7" aria-controls="a7" aria-haspopup="true" id="a7_Ctrl" role="button"><span>Caixia Li</span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a><span class="comma-separator">,&nbsp;</span><div class="author-info accordion-tabbed__content" data-db-target-of="a7" aria-labelledby="a7_Ctrl" role="region" id="a7">
                     <p class="author-name">Caixia Li</p>
                     <p>College of Sciences and Institute for Sustainable Energy, Shanghai University, Shanghai, 200444 China</p><a class="moreInfoLink" href="/authored-by/Li/Caixia">Search for more papers by this author</a></div></span><span class="accordion-tabbed__tab-mobile  accordion__closed"><a href="/authored-by/Wang/Ruixiao" class="author-name accordion-tabbed__control" data-id="a8" data-db-target-for="a8" aria-controls="a8" aria-haspopup="true" id="a8_Ctrl" role="button"><span>Ruixiao Wang</span><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-section_arrow_d"></i></a><span class="comma-separator">,&nbsp;</span><div class="author-info accordion-tabbed__content" data-db-target-of="a8" aria-labelledby="a8_Ctrl" role="region" id="a8">

   <div class="abstract-group ">
      <section class="article-section article-section__abstract" lang="en" data-lang="en" lang-name="English" id="section-1-en">
         <h2 id="d5949551" class="article-section__header section__title main abstractlang_en main">Abstract</h2>
         <div class="article-section__content en main">
            
            <p>Hard carbons, as one of the most commercializable anode materials for sodium-ion batteries (SIBs), have to deal with the trade-off between the rate capability and specific capacity or initial Columbic efficiency (ICE), and the fast performance decline at low temperature (LT) remains poorly understood. Here, a comprehensive regulation on the interfacial/bulk electrochemistry of hard carbons through atomic Zn doping is reported, which demonstrates a record-high reversible capacity (546 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>), decent ICE (84%), remarkable rate capability (140 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> @ 50 A g<sup>−1</sup>), and excellent LT capacity (443 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> @ −40 °C), outperforming the state-of-the-art literature. This work reveals that the Zn doping can generally induce a local electric field to enable fast bulk Na<sup>+</sup> transportation, and meanwhile catalyze the decomposition of NaPF<sub>6</sub> to form a robust inorganic-rich solid-electrolyte interphase, which elaborates the underlying origin of the boosted electrochemical performance. Importantly, distinguished from room temperature, the intrinsic Na<sup>+</sup> migration/desolvation ability of the electrolyte is disclosed to be the crucial rate-determining factors for the SIB performance at LT. This work provides a fundamental understanding on the charge-storage kinetics at varied temperatures.</p>
            </div>
      </section>
   </div>
   <div class="pb-dropzone" data-pb-dropzone="below-abstract-group"><!-- Empty dropzone --></div>
   
   <section class="article-section article-section__full">
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202211461-sec-0010">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202211461-sec-0010-title">1 Introduction</h2>
         
         <p>Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) are considered as one of the most competitive candidates for grid-scale energy storage devices owing to the abundant sodium resource, and their promising charge-storage capability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0001_R_d5949537e369" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Adv. Mater.">1</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Hard carbons (HCs) have attracted remarkable attention as the preferred SIB anode, which are reported to be capable of Na storage within suitable graphitic microdomains and nanopores.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0002_R_d5949537e374" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Chem. Eng. J.">2</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To date, numerous attempts have been made to improve the electrochemical performance of HCs, including expanding interlayer distance to enable fast (de)intercalation of Na<sup>+</sup> in the graphitic domains;<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0003" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0003_R_d5949537e382" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 3 - Nat. Commun.">3</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> optimizing the porous system to boost the Na<sup>+</sup>/Na cluster storage within suitable pores;<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0004_R_d5949537e389" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">4</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> as well as introducing heteroatoms (e.g., N,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0005_R_d5949537e395" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Energy Storage Mater.">5</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> S,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0006" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0006_R_d5949537e400" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 6 - Adv. Mater.">6</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> F,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0007" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0007_R_d5949537e405" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 7 - Energy Storage Mater.">7</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> etc.) or defects<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0008" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0008_R_d5949537e411" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 8 - Chem. Mater.">8</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> to provide more charge adsorption sites, etc.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0009" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0009_R_d5949537e416" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 9 - Small">9</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Recently, such efforts were summarized as the carbon p-band center manipulation to balance Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption energy and transportation barrier, which could be generally achieved by varying the carbon precursors or calcination temperatures.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0010_R_d5949537e424" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Mater.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, traditional approaches in manipulating the microstructure of HCs have encountered bottlenecks, and the trade-off between the rate performance, and initial Columbic efficiency (ICE) or specific capacity, as well as its unsatisfied low-temperature (LT) performance, remain challenging obstacles that hindered the practical applications of HCs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0011_R_d5949537e429" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Nat. Commun.">11</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
         
         <p>It is noticed that, the localized carbon structure can be readily modulated by introducing M–N<i><sub>x</sub></i>–C coordination (M, N, and C denoted as metal, nitrogen, and carbon atoms, respectively), which has been extensively investigated in electrocatalytic fields.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0012" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0012_R_d5949537e439" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 12 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">12</a>-<a href="#adma202211461-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0014_R_d5949537e439" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Some pioneer studies have introduced M–N<i><sub>x</sub></i>–C into carbon as electrode materials in Li-metal and Li–sulfur batteries<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0015" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0015_R_d5949537e447" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 15 - ACS Appl. Mater. Interfaces">15</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and Li-ion capacitors,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0016" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0016_R_d5949537e453" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 16 - Adv. Energy Mater.">16</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which could improve the Li affinity or trigger the surface mediated reaction of Li polysulfides.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0017" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0017_R_d5949537e458" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 17 - J. Am. Chem. Soc.">17</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0018" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0018_R_d5949537e458" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 18 - Adv. Energy Mater.">18</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Recent studies reported that the Fe–N<i><sub>x</sub></i>–C can enable the reversible conversions of solid-electrolyte interphase (SEI) for SIBs, showing a high capacity of 453 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>, nevertheless the ICE is relatively low due to its defect-rich structures.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0019_R_d5949537e469" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Energy Environ. Sci.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Some other researchers constructed a Zn–N–S architecture, which is considered to be capable of storing extra charge at the metal active sites with enhanced electrochemical performance for potassium ion batteries (KIBs).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0020" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0020_R_d5949537e474" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 20 - Matter">20</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> More recently, carbon microcuboids-supported Cu single atoms with a high Cu content of 26.3 wt% were investigated as the anode material for SIBs, which delivered a specific capacity of 107.7 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 5 A g<sup>−1</sup>.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0021_R_d5949537e484" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Adv. Energy Mater.">21</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Nevertheless, the electrochemical performance of the HCs is comprehensively affected by the bulk structure of the HC, the solvation structure of the electrolyte, as well as the SEI chemistry.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0011_R_d5949537e489" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Nat. Commun.">11</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0022_R_d5949537e489" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Nature">22</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To date, few HCs have been reported to demonstrate a high capacity, fast charging ability and long cycle stability simultaneously over a wide range temperature.</p>
         
         <p>Inspired by above studies, we herein report a hard carbon with atomically incorporated zinc single atoms (Zn-HC) to modulate the bulk and surface structure. The optimized Zn-HC features expanded graphite regions (<i>d</i><sub>002</sub> = 0.408&nbsp;nm) and highly developed nanopores (diameter of ≈0.8&nbsp;nm) and reduced defect content, which facilitates fast Na<sup>+</sup> storage. We confirm that, the Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C architecture can catalyze the rapid decomposing of NaPF<sub>6</sub> and enable a thin and inorganic-rich SEI and fast interfacial Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics, and meanwhile trigger a local electric field (LEF) within the graphitic domains, which provides an adventitious Coulombic force to accelerate bulk Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics with reduced diffusion barrier (0.60&nbsp;eV vs 1.10&nbsp;eV). The as obtained HC material demonstrates a record high reversible capacity (546 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> @ 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>), rate capability (140 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> @ 50 A g<sup>−1</sup>), ICE (84%), LT capacity (443 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> @ −40 °C), outperforming the state-of-the-art literatures. The as constructed full-cell delivers a high energy-density of 323&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> and a high power density of 7.02&nbsp;kW kg<sup>−1</sup> (based on the total active mass on both electrodes). Promisingly, the underlying factors that affect the sodium storage behaviors at varied temperatures from Room-temperature (RT, 25 °C) to −40&nbsp;°C are disclosed. This work demonstrates a fundamental explanation for the performance enhancing mechanism of the atomic metal doped HCs, and implies the possible ways to further improve the LT performance.</p>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202211461-sec-0020">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202211461-sec-0020-title">2 Results and Discussion</h2>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202211461-sec-0030">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adma202211461-sec-0030-title">2.1 Sample Preparation and Structural Characterization</h3>
            
            <p>Herein, atomic Zn-regulated HC (denoted as Zn-HC) was successfully synthesized via a typical two-step process including precursor synthesis and carbonization strategy, as illustrated in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1a</a>, in which a 2,4-diaminophenol formaldehyde resin (DAFR) served as C and N precursor, and zinc (II) acetate as Zn precursor, respectively. During the process, Zn<sup>2+</sup> was first coordinated with the –NH<sub>2</sub>– groups on DAFR chains thus dispersed homogeneously on DAFR chains (denoted as Zn-DAFR). The Zn-DAFR was further pyrolyzed at 1300 °C under argon protection to form the final product. By eliminating the Zn precursor, a control sample (denoted as HC) was prepared under the same condition (the details are provided in experimental procedures). Promisingly, such a synthesis strategy is distinguished from the template sacrificed synthesis methods,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0023" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0023_R_d5949537e550" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 23 - Adv. Energy Mater.">23</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> and applicable for the large-scale preparation of the HCs with well-regulated microstructures (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1a</a>, Supporting Information). The morphologies of the as prepared samples were characterized by scanning electron microscope (SEM), Zn-HC and the control sample possess the similar stacked microsphere morphology with smooth surface (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1b</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2a,b</a>, Supporting Information). From the high-angle annular dark-field scanning transmission electron microscopy (HAADF-STEM) image, myriad bright spots are observed and evenly distributed in the HC substrate (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1c</a>), revealing that the Zn species are atomically dispersed. High-resolution transmission electron microscopy (HRTEM) was employed to reveal the microstructure of the prepared samples, the Zn-HC appears short-ordered structure with larger interlayer distance (<i>d</i><sub>002</sub>) of 0.408&nbsp;nm (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1d</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2c</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a>, Supporting Information), which is considered favorable for the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0005_R_d5949537e584" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Energy Storage Mater.">5</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0024" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0024_R_d5949537e584" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 24 - ChemSusChem">24</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Unlike Zn-HC, the control sample presents more disordered structure with smaller interlayer distance (<i>d</i><sub>002</sub> <i>=</i> 0.384&nbsp;nm) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2d</a>, Supporting Information). Energy-dispersive X-ray spectroscopy (EDS) mapping image reveals that C, N, O, and Zn elements distribute uniformly over the substrate in Zn-HC (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2e</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202211461-fig-0001"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/d4ffd752-4253-496c-a983-b740883aea37/adma202211461-fig-0001-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/d4ffd752-4253-496c-a983-b740883aea37/adma202211461-fig-0001-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/64241e35-0146-44d7-9feb-8391d0cdc176/adma202211461-fig-0001-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/d4ffd752-4253-496c-a983-b740883aea37/adma202211461-fig-0001-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 1<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202211461-fig-0001&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202211461" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Morphological structure characterizations and atomistic structure analysis for Zn-HC. a) Schematic illustration of the synthesis for Zn-HC. b) SEM image. c) Aberration-corrected HAADF-STEM image. d) HRTEM image. e) Zn K-edge XANES. f) Fourier-transform EXAFS spectra. g) Wavelet transform of the <i>k</i><sup>2</sup>-weighted EXAFS data. h) Comparison of <i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub>, <i>Lc</i>, <i>La</i>, and <i>d</i><sub>002</sub>. i) Comparison of pore size distribution.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) was investigated to characterize chemical composition and elemental status (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). It is noted that, Zn-HC exhibits a remarkable increase of N content (4.30 at%) over HC (1.12 at%) (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information), implying the possibility of anchoring sites for the immobilization of Zn atoms.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0014" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0014_R_d5949537e649" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 14 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">14</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, XPS results confirm the existence of Zn in Zn-HC (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3a,b</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S2</a>, Supporting Information). The bulk elemental information for the samples were further examined by inductively coupled plasma mass spectrometry (ICP-MS) for Zn (0.73 wt%; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S3</a>, Supporting Information), and organic element analysis method for C, N, O (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S4</a>, Supporting Information). X-ray absorption near-edge structure (XANES) and extended X-ray absorption fine structure (EXAFS) measurements were conducted to further elucidate the dispersion state and coordination configuration of Zn in Zn-HC (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1e–g</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0025" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0025_R_d5949537e674" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 25 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">25</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1e</a>, the adsorption edge position of Zn-HC is far away from that of Zn foil and meanwhile at lower energy than that of ZnO/ZnPc. No Zn<span class="icomoon"></span>Zn bonding at 2.32 Å is detected that excludes the presence of metallic Zn in Zn-HC and underlines good atom dispersion of Zn sites (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1f</a>). To further verify the atomic dispersion of the Zn species, the EXAFS wavelet transform (WT) analysis was conducted as it can provide both radial distance and <i>k</i>-space resolution of backscattering atoms (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1g</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0026" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0026_R_d5949537e691" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 26 - Small">26</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Distinguishing from the Zn–Zn scattering at ≈7.0 Å<sup>−1</sup> presented in Zn foil, Zn-HC displays only one peak with maximum intensity at ≈4.2 Å<sup>−1</sup>, which can be assigned to the Zn–N contributions, excluding the possible formation of Zn-derived nanoparticles. Besides, the Zn EXAFS spectra of Zn-HC is similar to that of ZnPc, suggesting their analogous bonding configuration, and the first-shell main peaks at 1.59 Å for Zn-HC and 1.56 Å for ZnPc, are attributed to Zn–N coordination (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1f</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0027" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0027_R_d5949537e704" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 27 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">27</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The coordination configuration was further extracted by quantitative least-squares EXAFS fitting (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S5</a>, Supporting Information), which indicates the coordination number of Zn to N is ≈4.0, confirming the Zn–N<sub>4</sub> coordination.</p>
            
            <p>X-ray diffraction patterns (XRD) for both samples display typical diffraction patterns of hard carbon (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6b,c</a>, Supporting Information),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0002_R_d5949537e723" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Chem. Eng. J.">2</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0019_R_d5949537e723" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Energy Environ. Sci.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> with calculated <i>d</i><sub>002</sub> of 0.404&nbsp;nm for Zn-HC and 0.383&nbsp;nm for HC respectively. The parameters obtained from various characterization techniques are compared in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1h</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1</a> (Supporting Information). The density functional theory (DFT) calculation results further confirm that Zn doping in HCs could enlarge the interlayer distance by 5.4% (3.33–3.53 Å) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7a,b</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0005" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0005_R_d5949537e741" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 5 - Energy Storage Mater.">5</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0028" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0028_R_d5949537e741" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 28 - Adv. Energy Mater.">28</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Raman spectra further suggest less defects of Zn-HC than HC (<i>I</i><sub>D</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub> of 0.97&nbsp;vs 1.04) due to the Zn atoms efficiently catalyze the graphitization during calcination (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1h</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>de, Supporting Information),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0019_R_d5949537e759" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Energy Environ. Sci.">19</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which could boost the ICE of SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0029_R_d5949537e765" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The pore structure and specific surface area (SSA) of prepared samples were evaluated by nitrogen (de)sorption isotherms (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1i</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information), the Zn-HC exhibits enriched microporous structure mainly range from 0.8 to 1.2&nbsp;nm (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1i</a>), with higher total pore volume (0.048 cm<sup>3</sup> g<sup>−1</sup>) than the control sample (0.036 cm<sup>3</sup> g<sup>−1</sup>) (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information), which might be ascribed to the reaction between partial Zn species and around carbon during calcination.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0030" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0030_R_d5949537e791" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 30 - Mater. Des.">30</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It is considered favorable for the Na<sup>+</sup> filling in the electrochemical test.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0031_R_d5949537e799" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - npj Comput. Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The specific surface area (SSA) is calculated as 103.68 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>−1</sup> for Zn-HC, which is slightly higher than that of HC (90.75 m<sup>2</sup> g<sup>−1</sup>) (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S6</a>, Supporting Information). The enlarged interlayer distance, reduced defects and moderate SSA and pore volume caused by the atomic Zn doping, can simultaneously enable a high Na<sup>+</sup> storage capacity and a high ICE for Zn-HC in the electrochemical test.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202211461-sec-0040">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adma202211461-sec-0040-title">2.2 Sodium Storage Performance</h3>
            
            <p>The electrochemical performances of the samples were revealed by Na||HC half-cells operated with a conventional sodic ether-based electrolytes (1&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub> in diethylene glycol dimethyl ether (diglyme)). First, the cyclic voltammetry (CV) measurement was performed to analyze the electrochemical behavior of the as prepared samples in the voltage range of 0.01–2.0&nbsp;V.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0032" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0032_R_d5949537e831" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 32 - Small Sci.">32</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0033_R_d5949537e831" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Adv. Energy Mater.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9a</a> (Supporting Information) shows a pair of sharp redox peaks at ≈0.10&nbsp;V/0.02&nbsp;V for Zn-HC at a scan rate of 0.2&nbsp;mV s<sup>−1</sup>, respectively, corresponding to the plateau region below 0.1&nbsp;V due to the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation within the graphitic layers or Na filling in the nanopores.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0001_R_d5949537e844" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Adv. Mater.">1</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0002" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0002_R_d5949537e844" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 2 - Chem. Eng. J.">2</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0033" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0033_R_d5949537e844" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 33 - Adv. Energy Mater.">33</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The first discharge/charge (GCD) curves of Zn-HC and HC at potential window of 0.01–2&nbsp;V are shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202211461-fig-0002">2a</a>, both curves present a sloping region above 0.1&nbsp;V and a plateau region below 0.1&nbsp;V in discharge curves. Notably, an obvious charge plateau at 0.5&nbsp;V is observed which should be attributed to the redox reaction between Na<sup>+</sup> and CO group, as evidenced by ex situ XPS spectra (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10a–d</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0001_R_d5949537e861" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Adv. Mater.">1</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0010_R_d5949537e861" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Mater.">10</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Zn-HC demonstrates a record high reversible capacity 65/546 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at the current density of 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>, with a corresponding ICE of 84%. As contrast, the discharge/charge capacities of the control sample are 495/363, with a much lower ICE of 73% (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, Supporting Information). Moreover, 65% of the specific capacity of Zn-HC electrode is contributed by the plateau region (0.01–0.1&nbsp;V) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11a</a>, Supporting Information), which would benefit the full-cell construction.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0034" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0034_R_d5949537e877" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 34 - Adv. Mater.">34</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0035" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0035_R_d5949537e877" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 35 - Small">35</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> The Zn-HC electrode with high mass loading (6.81&nbsp;mg cm<sup>−2</sup>) was also tested as shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11c,d</a> (Supporting Information). Moreover, both rate and cycling tests were conducted for Zn-HC and HC electrodes (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0002">2b,d</a>; Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11e</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12a,b</a>, Supporting Information), whereby the charging capacities of the Zn-HC electrode are higher than the HC electrode at all rates, and achieves highly reversible charge capacities of 542, 451, 402, 335, 302, 198, and 140 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> from 0.05 to 50 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S7</a>, Supporting Information), indicating the ultrafast Na<sup>+</sup> reaction kinetics of Zn-HC.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0001_R_d5949537e907" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Adv. Mater.">1</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0036_R_d5949537e907" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Adv. Mater.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As contrast, the control sample only delivers a capacity of 78 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 20 A g<sup>−1</sup>. Furthermore, the Zn-HC electrode demonstrates an outstanding cycling stability with 90% capacity retention after 3800 cycles at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup> (305.3 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) and 77% after 5000 cycles (270.4 mAh g<sup>−1</sup>) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0002">2d</a>), Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11f</a> (Supporting Information) shows the corresponding GCD curves of different cycles (including the 1st, 1500th and 3000th cycles), revealing the excellent voltage stability performance of Zn-HC electrode during repeated charge/discharge processes. This is significantly superior to the control sample, which is only 233 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 1000 cycles at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup> (76% capacity retention) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0002">2d</a>). Such a high capacity, rate capability, cycling stability and ICE outperform the state-of-the-art anode materials reported in literature, manifesting the Zn-HC composite is a promising anode material for SIBs (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0002">2c,e</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S8</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0001" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0001_R_d5949537e943" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 1 - Adv. Mater.">1</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0019_R_d5949537e943" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Energy Environ. Sci.">19</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0021" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0021_R_d5949537e943" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 21 - Adv. Energy Mater.">21</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0036_R_d5949537e943" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Adv. Mater.">36</a>-<a href="#adma202211461-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0040_R_d5949537e943" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S1b</a> (Supporting Information) also shows that a NVP (Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub>) || Zn-HC pouch cell can light up 52 LED bulbs.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202211461-fig-0002"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/0d442b31-9acb-42e1-ac84-0f309f9f1ddf/adma202211461-fig-0002-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/0d442b31-9acb-42e1-ac84-0f309f9f1ddf/adma202211461-fig-0002-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/9055338a-605d-4f8e-8d11-1031d087ab95/adma202211461-fig-0002-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/0d442b31-9acb-42e1-ac84-0f309f9f1ddf/adma202211461-fig-0002-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 2<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202211461-fig-0002&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202211461" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Electrochemical characterization for Zn-HC and HC at room temperature (25 °C). a) The first cycle of GCD curves in the potential range of 0.01–2.00&nbsp;V at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>. b) Rate capabilities. c) Comparison of rate capability with the typical carbon anodes reported previously. d) Cycling stabilities. e) Comparison of ICE and cycle number with the typical carbon anodes reported previously. Low-temperature performance (−40 °C). f) The GCD curves (the second cycle). g) Cycling stabilities. h) Comparison of LT capacity with the typical anodes reported previously.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The low-temperature (LT) performance of the samples were tested at an extremely low temperature (−40 °C) to simulate the actual application scenario. A remarkably high charge capacity of 443 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> is achieved for Zn-HC at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup> current density (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0002">2f</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13a–d</a>, Supporting Information). Moreover, the Zn-HC electrode maintains a stable cycling performance at LT (258 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> after 400 cycles) with a capacity retention of 85% (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0002">2g</a>). On the contrary, the HC sample cannot withstand a cycling test of 100 cycles at −40&nbsp;°C (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0002">2g</a>). Such an LT performance is superior to that of the control sample HC and the state-of-the-art anode materials for SIBs (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0002">2h</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S9</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0041" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0041_R_d5949537e1010" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 41 - Chem. Eng. J.">41</a>-<a href="#adma202211461-bib-0049" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0049_R_d5949537e1010" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 49 - Nano Energy">49</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This might be attributed to that the single-atom-Zn doped architecture could optimize the electrolyte/electrode interface, thus suppress the growth of Na dendrites, and significantly improve its LT cycling stability.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202211461-sec-0050">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adma202211461-sec-0050-title">2.3 Understanding the Role of Atomic Zn-Doping for the Na Storage Behavior</h3>
            
            <p>Transmission electron microscopy (TEM) was used to analyze the microstructures of the SEI layer after cycling at RT, the thickness of the SEI layer formed on the Zn-HC surface (5&nbsp;nm) is much thinner than that of HC (11&nbsp;nm) after 200 cycles (<b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3a,b</a>), which benefits the faster interfacial Na<sup>+</sup> transportation kinetics, and contributes to higher ICE and rate capability. HRTEM images (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3a</a>) indicate more uniform and thinner SEI layer of Zn-HC electrode, which can be divided into an amorphous outer layer and a crystalline inorganic inner layer with some randomly distributed nanocrystals featuring the lattice fringe distance of 0.24&nbsp;nm, corresponding to the (200) face of NaF (corresponding to the yellow rectangular area in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3a</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0036_R_d5949537e1039" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Adv. Mater.">36</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0050_R_d5949537e1039" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small Sci.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It has been reported that the inorganic component such as NaF presents lower Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion activation energies (100–150 meV) than organic species,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0051" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0051_R_d5949537e1046" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 51 - Nat. Commun.">51</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which effectively facilitate interfacial Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics and improve the mechanical strength of SEI layer.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0052_R_d5949537e1054" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Surprisingly, the SEI layer on Zn-HC after 600 cycles retain stable with the thickness almost unchanged at RT (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16a</a>, Supporting Information), the uniform and thin SEI layer is consistent with the low and stable <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> (resistance in SEI layers) value (<b>Figure</b>&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4a,c</a>) that accounts for the fast interfacial Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics and stable long-term cycling at RT.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0019_R_d5949537e1074" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Energy Environ. Sci.">19</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0053_R_d5949537e1074" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Small Sci.">53</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> In contrast, the control sample possesses a thicker and non-uniform SEI layer (≈11&nbsp;nm) with mixed organic and inorganic components after 200 cycles at RT (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3b</a>). Such a simply mixed thick SEI could neither stabilize the HC electrode nor suppress the repeated formation of SEI during cycling. Even worse, the SEI layer on HC electrode evolves into irregular chunks of aggregates with a thickness over 20&nbsp;nm after 600 cycles (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S16b</a>, Supporting Information), which might account for the poor rate performance and cycling stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0050_R_d5949537e1086" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small Sci.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Interestingly, Zn-HC electrode shows an even thinner SEI with a thickness of 3&nbsp;nm after 200 cycles at LT (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3c</a>), indicating the SEI thickness might not the determining factor for the LT performance decay.</p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202211461-fig-0003"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/a87b5367-dbc3-41f3-ba6d-a1a8414d741b/adma202211461-fig-0003-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/a87b5367-dbc3-41f3-ba6d-a1a8414d741b/adma202211461-fig-0003-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/e0d19ecb-1a50-4e67-97f1-0df82debf58b/adma202211461-fig-0003-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/a87b5367-dbc3-41f3-ba6d-a1a8414d741b/adma202211461-fig-0003-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 3<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202211461-fig-0003&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202211461" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a,b) HRTEM images of Zn-HC and HC electrodes (0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, 200th cycle, 25 °C). c) HRTEM image of Zn-HC electrode (0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, 200th cycle, −40 °C). d) XPS spectra of F 1s of the formed SEI layers on Zn-HC and HC (0.1 A g<sup>−1</sup>, 2th cycle, 25 °C). e) <i>E</i><sub>d</sub> of the P<span class="icomoon"></span>F bond for Zn-HC and HC electrode interfaces. f) Diffusion barrier energies for Zn-HC-Gra and HC-Gra. g) <i>E</i><sub>a</sub> and <i>E</i><sub>b</sub> for Zn-HC-Gra and HC-Gra. h) Isosurface of charge density difference and planar-average charge density plot of Zn-HC-Gra. The cyan and yellow regions refer to electron accumulation and depletion, respectively. The isosurface is 0.0027 e Bohr<sup>−3</sup>. i) The schematic diagram of the enhanced rate capability mechanism.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202211461-fig-0004"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/e459fb72-1306-45d7-b07c-fd917c2dd4e5/adma202211461-fig-0004-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/e459fb72-1306-45d7-b07c-fd917c2dd4e5/adma202211461-fig-0004-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/4fd38a2f-58c8-4f01-a22b-553ff716ea64/adma202211461-fig-0004-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/e459fb72-1306-45d7-b07c-fd917c2dd4e5/adma202211461-fig-0004-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 4<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202211461-fig-0004&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202211461" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">Charge-storage kinetics analysis for Zn-HC and HC at varied temperatures. a,b) Zn-HC and HC electrodes during two-electrode operando-EIS measurements at 25 °C. c) The evolution of <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of Zn-HC and HC electrodes during cycling at 25 °C. d) Zn-HC and HC electrodes during two-electrode operando-EIS measurements after ten cycles at 25 and −40 °C. e) Comparison of <i>R</i><sub>s</sub>, <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of Zn-HC and HC electrodes after ten cycles at 25 and −40 °C. f) Arrhenius curves and the calculated activation energies for <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> as obtained from the Nyquist plots of the Zn-HC and HC electrodes. g) Comparison of charge-storage kinetics behavior at 25 and −40 °C.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
            <p>The components of SEI layers were analyzed by ex situ XPS spectra (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17</a>, Supporting Information). Similar organic-inorganic hybrid SEI structures are formed on Zn-HC and HC electrodes during cycling at RT. According to XPS C 1s, O 1s and F 1s spectra of SEI layers on Zn-HC and HC surfaces, the characteristic peaks of polyether (284.56&nbsp;eV) and C─O/O─H (531.08&nbsp;eV) belong to the diglyme solvent (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17a–d</a>, Supporting Information),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0036_R_d5949537e1183" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Adv. Mater.">36</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> R─CH<sub>2</sub>─O─Na (284.06&nbsp;eV) was assigned to the NaPF<sub>6</sub>-solvent complex reductions (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S17a,b</a>, Supporting Information), Na─F (683.7&nbsp;eV) could be originated from reductive decomposition of PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> anion solvates (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3d</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0050_R_d5949537e1202" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small Sci.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Notably, the SEI layers of Zn-HC surfaces show higher Na-F (25.4%) concentration than HC (12.1%) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3d</a>). Therefore, a thin and uniform NaF-dominated SEI can form on Zn-HC electrode in NaPF<sub>6</sub>–diglyme electrolyte. To understand this phenomenon, DFT calculation was conducted by constructing a Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C configuration in the graphene plane of a 4 × 4 supercell (denoted as Zn-HC-SLG) to simulate the dissociation process of NaPF<sub>6</sub> on Zn-HC surface and the SEI formation (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S18a–c</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0052" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0052_R_d5949537e1221" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 52 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">52</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> It reveals that, the Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C configuration decreases the dissociation energy (<i>E</i><sub>d</sub>) for P<span class="icomoon"></span>F bond breaking (1.62&nbsp;eV) on the Zn-HC surface compared to the vacancy defects (HC-SLG, 2.55&nbsp;eV) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3e</a>), demonstrating that the Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C configuration promotes decomposition of NaPF<sub>6</sub> and boosts Na<sup>+</sup> to react with electron-rich F and form NaF compounds and dispersed evenly, which is consistent with F 1s spectra of SEI layers on Zn-HC electrode (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3d</a>).</p>
            
            <p>In situ electrochemical impedance spectra (EIS) was used to explore SEI evolution and interface dynamics for Zn-HC and HC electrodes. All electrochemical impedance spectra were fitted with the simplified equivalent circuits (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19</a>, Supporting Information), and the impedance data of each part after fitting are all summarized in Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S10</a> (Supporting Information). As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19a</a> (Supporting Information), for Zn-HC electrode, the impedance is soaring at 0.9&nbsp;V which could be attributed to the electrolyte decomposition, and then gradually stabilized, demonstrating that stable SEI is formed. Notably, the <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> (the resistance for Na<sup>+</sup> across SEI) and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (charge transfer resistance) values of Zn-HC electrode are prone to become smaller and more stable below 0.9&nbsp;V (&lt;5 Ω; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19c</a>, Supporting Information), indicating the thin and robust SEI on Zn-HC electrode surface, which is in agreement with the TEM image (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3a</a>). On the contrary, the <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values of HC are much larger and waved below 0.9&nbsp;V (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S19b,d</a>, Supporting Information), suggesting the unstable and thicker SEI on the HC electrode.</p>
            
            <p>As is well known that the Na<sup>+</sup> transfer behavior in SEI layer has significant effect on the overall electrochemical reaction kinetics. Generally, the solvated Na<sup>+</sup> will desolvate and diffuse across the SEI, and such process is highly dependent on the electrolyte and SEI chemistry.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0053" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0053_R_d5949537e1289" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 53 - Small Sci.">53</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0054_R_d5949537e1289" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - ACS Mater. Lett.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Inorganic-rich SEI layers are known to be more dense and sustainable, which can effectively protect the further breakdown of the electrolyte and improve cycle stability.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0037" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0037_R_d5949537e1294" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 37 - ACS Energy Lett.">37</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0055_R_d5949537e1294" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Adv. Mater.">55</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0056_R_d5949537e1294" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Especially, NaF inorganic species has an electronically insulating and low diffusion barrier for Na<sup>+</sup>,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0036" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0036_R_d5949537e1302" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 36 - Adv. Mater.">36</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0056_R_d5949537e1302" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> which can effectively prevent electrons form entering into the SEI and boost the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics. In addition, the uniform layered SEI could also be beneficial to the Na<sup>+</sup> desolvation behavior.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0057_R_d5949537e1312" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci. USA">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Therefore, such uniform and thin NaF-rich SEI structure on Zn-HC electrode induced by Zn doping could enable a fast charge transportation kinetics on the electrode/electrolyte interfaces.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0010_R_d5949537e1317" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Mater.">10</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0019" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0019_R_d5949537e1317" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 19 - Energy Environ. Sci.">19</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0040" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0040_R_d5949537e1317" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 40 - ACS Sustainable Chem. Eng.">40</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <p>On the other hand, DFT calculations were also performed to understand the effect of Zn atom on the Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics. According to the microstructural features of Zn-HC and HC (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0001">1h,i</a>), a representative double layer graphite (DLG, AB stacking) of 5 × 5 supercell and a 15 Å vacuum space along the y-axis was considered to simulate the Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation in the graphitic domains of both Zn-HC and HC (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0010_R_d5949537e1334" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Mater.">10</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0029" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0029_R_d5949537e1334" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 29 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">29</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Vacancy defects (VD) were introduced into the DLG model to manipulate the graphitic domain of the samples in practical conditions (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S20b,e</a>, Supporting Information), denoted as HC-Gra for HC and Zn-HC-Gra for Zn-HC respectively. The climbing-image nudged elastic band (CINEB) method was used to evaluate the energy barrier (<i>E</i><sub>b</sub>) for Na<sup>+</sup> migration (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3f</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S21</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0054" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0054_R_d5949537e1355" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 54 - ACS Mater. Lett.">54</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As expected, the Zn-HC-Gra exhibits a moderate absorption energy and a significantly reduced Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion energy barrier values (0.60&nbsp;eV) than HC-Gra (1.10&nbsp;eV) (Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a>, Supporting Information), which benefits the fast bulk Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion in the graphitic domains, representing one of the main factors for its excellent rate capability. The Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption energy (<i>E</i><sub>a</sub>) and <i>E</i><sub>b</sub> for Zn-HC and HC in the nanopores with different environments were also simulated and compared in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3g</a>, and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S22–S24</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S11</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a> (Supporting Information), which indicates that the Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C architecture benefit the Na<sup>+</sup> storage in both graphitic layers and nanopores.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0004" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0004_R_d5949537e1393" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 4 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">4</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0031" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0031_R_d5949537e1393" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 31 - npj Comput. Mater.">31</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> To get an in-depth understanding on this phenomenon, the charge density difference and the corresponding planar-average charge density around the Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C configuration were calculated. As depicted in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3h</a> and Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S25</a> (Supporting Information), cyan and yellow regions refer to electron accumulation and depletion, respectively, the Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C configuration induces the lopsided charge distribution from Zn to adjacent N atoms. Eventually, the Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C configuration possesses an electron-richer environment, and triggers an in-plane LEF which serves as a promoter to enhance the bulk Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics of Zn-HC as proved by the lower diffusion energy barrier (<i>E</i><sub>b,Zn-HC</sub> &lt; <i>E</i><sub>b,HC</sub>) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3g–h</a>).</p>
            
            <p>By combining the experimental observations and DFT analysis, a possible mechanism for the enhanced Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics in Zn-HC is proposed and illustrated in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3i</a> and Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a> (Supporting Information). Thanks to the ultrathin NaF-polymeric SEI layers contributed by interfacial catalysis of Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C configuration and in situ induced LEF by Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C configuration, both the bulk and interfacial Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics are enhanced significantly, leading to the unprecedented rate capability and ICE of Zn-HC electrode. Besides, the moderate adsorption energy and robust inorganic rich SEI can suppress the formation of Na dendrites, thus enabling the long cycle performance at LT environment.</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202211461-sec-0060">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adma202211461-sec-0060-title">2.4 Comprehensive Understanding on the Sodium Storage Mechanism at RT/LT through GITT and EIS Analysis</h3>
            
            <p>A detailed charge-storage kinetics analysis was conducted to gain a comprehensive insight on the sodium storage mechanism of the samples at both RT and LT. The galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) test was carried out to calculate the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients (<span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/24b11ded-b52a-4aa2-a2e7-8ce38656b62e/adma202211461-math-0001.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma202211461:adma202211461-math-0001" display="inline" location="graphic/adma202211461-math-0001.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>D</mi>
                        <msup>
                           <mi>Na</mi>
                           <mo>+</mo>
                        </msup>
                     </msub>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${D}_{{\rm{Na}}^{\rm{ + }}}$</annotation>
                  </semantics></math>) and evaluate the Na<sup>+</sup> storage kinetics in the bulk electrode at both 25 and −40 °C.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0055" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0055_R_d5949537e1464" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 55 - Adv. Mater.">55</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> As shown in Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26a,b</a> (Supporting Information), the <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/1baabcaa-03d0-4be0-9093-f3f653e3aff9/adma202211461-math-0002.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma202211461:adma202211461-math-0002" display="inline" location="graphic/adma202211461-math-0002.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>D</mi>
                        <msup>
                           <mi>Na</mi>
                           <mo>+</mo>
                        </msup>
                     </msub>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${D}_{{\rm{Na}}^{\rm{ + }}}$</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> values of the Zn-HC electrode (10<sup>−6.81</sup> to 10<sup>−5.50</sup>) are significantly enhanced as compared to the HC control sample (10<sup>−8.54</sup> to 10<sup>−6.75</sup>) under RT at all potentials, which agrees well with the superiority of Zn-HC in rate capability at RT (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S12</a>, Supporting Information) and supports the positive effect of Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C configuration on the kinetics of sodium storage.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0056" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0056_R_d5949537e1497" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 56 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">56</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> However, the <span class="fallback__mathEquation" data-altimg="/cms/asset/1db8920f-3417-41c2-857b-a4258c328426/adma202211461-math-0003.png"></span><math altimg="urn:x-wiley:09359648:media:adma202211461:adma202211461-math-0003" display="inline" location="graphic/adma202211461-math-0003.png">
                  <semantics>
                     <msub>
                        <mi>D</mi>
                        <msup>
                           <mi>Na</mi>
                           <mo>+</mo>
                        </msup>
                     </msub>
                     <annotation encoding="application/x-tex">${D}_{{\rm{Na}}^{\rm{ + }}}$</annotation>
                  </semantics></math> values at LT are slightly reduced for both Zn-HC (10<sup>−7.04</sup> to 10<sup>−6.01</sup>) and HC (10<sup>−8.87</sup> to 10<sup>−6.97</sup>) (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S26c,d</a>, Supporting Information). This indicates that, the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics within the electrode has been significantly improved at both RT and LT due to the atomic Zn doping. Therefore, further understandings are needed to explain the unsatisfied LT rate capability of Zn-HC (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S13</a>, Supporting Information).</p>
            
            <p>EIS measurements were conducted to investigate the interfacial charge transfer kinetics in Zn-HC/HC electrodes and SEI layer evolution during cycling at both 25 and −40 °C.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0050_R_d5949537e1532" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small Sci.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Selected Nyquist plots for Zn-HC and HC electrodes were presented in Figure <a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4a,b</a>, in which two semicircles and a straight line are identified in all these spectra, indicating the similar electrochemical processes in Zn-HC and HC electrodes. The <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> corresponds to the internal resistance including the resistances of the electrolyte solution and electrodes, while the semicircles at high and medium frequency are attributed to <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (including the Na<sup>+</sup>-deslovation process),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0050_R_d5949537e1552" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small Sci.">50</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0057_R_d5949537e1552" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci. USA">57</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> respectively. The <i>R</i><sub>s</sub>, <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values were quantified with an equivalent circuit (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4a,b</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information). As shown in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4a–c</a>, it could be found that the <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> in Zn-HC electrode are more stable (&lt;20 Ω) and greatly lower than those of HC after various cycles. For example, after 50 cycles, the <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> for HC (70 and 44 Ω) are 8.75 and 3.14 times that of Zn-HC (8 and 14 Ω), respectively at RT (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4c</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S14</a>, Supporting Information), verifying that the atomic Zn doping could enable a sustainably stable SEI on Zn-HC electrode surface and enhance the interfacial charge transfer kinetics.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0050" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0050_R_d5949537e1596" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 50 - Small Sci.">50</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <p>EIS measurements were also carried out for Zn-HC and HC electrodes at −40 °C. The Nyquist plots in Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4d</a> (local enlarged view) indicate the increase in <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> (10&nbsp;vs 34/35 Ω for Zn-HC/HC), suggesting the transfer ability of solvated Na<sup>+</sup> ions within the electrolyte deteriorate at LT environment which could be attributed to the increased viscosity of electrolyte at LT. Interestingly, the <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> variations from RT to LT for both Zn-HC (3&nbsp;vs 5 Ω) and HC (17&nbsp;vs 21 Ω) electrode are tiny, indicating the SEI composition is not the dominant factor affecting the LT charge transfer kinetics (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4d,e</a>).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0058_R_d5949537e1619" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Nat. Energy">58</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0059" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0059_R_d5949537e1619" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 59 - Nano Energy">59</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This is in well agreement with the small SEI thickness at LT as observed in TEM analysis (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0003">3c</a>). On the contrary, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> values for both Zn-HC (7&nbsp;vs 105 Ω) and HC (35&nbsp;vs 255 Ω) electrode were drastically elevated from RT to LT (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4d,e</a>), indicating the Na<sup>+</sup> desolvation barrier in Zn-HC electrode at LT is significantly increased, which might be the rate-determining step for the LT charge transfer in SIBs.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0048_R_d5949537e1636" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">48</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0060" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0060_R_d5949537e1636" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 60 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">60</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> This explains the phenomenon that, even though the micro-structure regulation can significantly reduce the <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> of Zn-HC electrode, the rate capability at LT is significantly reduced, which is more dependent on the intrinsic property of the electrolyte. Temperature-dependent EIS further confirms that the Na<sup>+</sup> desolvation barrier is significantly increased at LT (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4f</a>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S27</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S28</a>, Supporting Information),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0058" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0058_R_d5949537e1656" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 58 - Nat. Energy">58</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0061_R_d5949537e1656" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - ACS Energy Lett.">61</a>-<a href="#adma202211461-bib-0063" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0063_R_d5949537e1656" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 63 - Chemistry">63</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> manifesting that the activation energy of charge transfer process for Zn-HC (<i>E</i><sub>ac,ct,Zn-HC</sub> = 192 meV) is higher than that in the Na<sup>+</sup> transportation across SEI (<i>E</i><sub>ac,SEI,Zn-HC</sub> = 81 meV) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4f</a>).
