It is noticed that, both <i>E</i><sub>ac,SEI</sub> and <i>E</i><sub>ac,ct</sub> for Zn-HC (<i>E</i><sub>ac,SEI,Zn-HC</sub> = 81 meV, <i>E</i><sub>ac,ct,Zn-HC</sub> = 192 meV) has been significantly reduced as compared to that of HC (<i>E</i><sub>ac,SEI,HC</sub> = 100 meV, <i>E</i><sub>ac,ct,HC</sub> = 207 meV) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4f</a>), suggesting that the regulated HC microstructure by Zn doping can effectively reduce the activation energy of both Na<sup>+</sup> across the SEI and Na<sup>+</sup> transfer from electrolyte to the electrode. However, another phenomenon is ineligible, that the <i>E</i><sub>ac,ct</sub> values for both Zn-HC and HC are about twice that of <i>E</i><sub>ac,SEI</sub> indicating the intrinsic Na<sup>+</sup> desolvation in the electrolyte may be the dominate reason for the LT performance and could affect the rate capability at LT. To verify this presumption, we reasonably reduced the concentration of NaPF<sub>6</sub> to 0.5&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span>, thus achieving a much lower viscosity of electrolyte at LT (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S29</a>, Supporting Information),<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0048" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0048_R_d5949537e1717" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 48 - Angew. Chem., Int. Ed.">48</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> obviously, the <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> (130&nbsp;vs 34 Ω) and <i>R</i><sub>s</sub> (34&nbsp;vs 13 Ω) values for Zn-HC electrode are indeed effectively decreased (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30a</a>, Supporting Information). As a result, Zn-HC electrode presents superior LT performance at a higher rate in 0.5&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub>–diglyme than 1.0&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub>–diglyme (398&nbsp;vs 286 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.2 A g<sup>−1</sup>; Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30b</a>, Supporting Information), and suppressed voltage polarization on the GCD curves (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S30b</a>, Supporting Information). Bearing this in mind, we further tested the desolvation activation energy of Zn-HC electrode with 0.5&nbsp;<span class="smallCaps">m</span> NaPF<sub>6</sub>–diglyme,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0057" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0057_R_d5949537e1756" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 57 - Proc. Natl. Acad. Sci. USA">57</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0064" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0064_R_d5949537e1756" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 64 - ACS Energy Lett.">64</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> of which <i>E</i><sub>a,ct</sub> was reduced to137 meV (Figure <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S31a</a>, Supporting Information). Therefore, we suggest that, the Na<sup>+</sup> desolvation process could possibly be the rate-determining step for Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics at LT and the increased viscosity of electrolyte would affect LT performance.<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0011" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0011_R_d5949537e1772" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 11 - Nat. Commun.">11</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0022" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0022_R_d5949537e1772" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 22 - Nature">22</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0061" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0061_R_d5949537e1772" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 61 - ACS Energy Lett.">61</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0062" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0062_R_d5949537e1772" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 62 - ACS Energy Lett.">62</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <p>Combining the experiment and calculation results, we can conclude that, the unprecedented rate capability and ICE of Zn-HC at RT should be attributed to the synergy between faster interfacial and bulk storage kinetics which could be induced by Zn doping. First, the well-regulated HC consists of graphitic domains with larger interlayer distance (<i>d</i><sub>002</sub> = 0.408&nbsp;nm) and adjustable nanopore structures (nanopore diameter of 0.8–1.2&nbsp;nm), which are prerequisites for Na<sup>+</sup> intercalation and Na clustering upon charge/discharge. Second, the Zn–N<sub>4</sub>–C configuration not only induces the in-plane LEF to improve bulk Na transportation kinetics, but also accelerates the rapid decomposing of NaPF<sub>6</sub> to enable an ultrathin SEI with inorganic-rich species (NaF) and promote faster interfacial Na transportation kinetics, eventually favoring superior rate capability and high ICE at RT. Note that, though the ideally thin and robust SEI and optimized bulk structure of HCs could boost the Na<sup>+</sup> storage and transportation ability at low rates under LT environment, the LT capacity at high rates retarded drastically, which could possibly be attributed to sluggish Na<sup>+</sup> desolvation kinetics and the increased viscosity of electrolytes at LT. Therefore, to develop high performance SIBs over a wide range of temperature, an advanced electrolyte featuring with weak Na<sup>+</sup>-solvent interactions, low viscosity and satisfied SEI is highly desired (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0004">4g</a>).</p>
            </section>
         
         <section class="article-section__sub-content" id="adma202211461-sec-0070">
            
            <h3 class="article-section__sub-title section2" id="adma202211461-sec-0070-title">2.5 Electrochemical Characterizations of the Zn-HC||NVP Coin Cells</h3>
            
            <p>To evaluate the practical application possibility of Zn-HC in the diglyme-based electrolytes, the full-cell was assembled and corresponding configuration is shown in <b>Figure</b> <a href="#adma202211461-fig-0005">5a</a>, using Zn-HC as anode and NVP as cathode, and tested at 0.05–10 A g<sup>−1</sup> in a potential range of 1.5–3.9&nbsp;V at both 25 and −40 °C. Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0005">5b</a> demonstrates that the assembled full cell can power 52 light emitting diode (LED) bulbs in series. It should be noted that, the full cell delivers a high charge capacity of 524 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup> (based on the active mass of the anode material) with an average working potential of 3.3&nbsp;V (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0005">5c</a>) under 25 °C,<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0065" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0065_R_d5949537e1827" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 65 - Adv. Funct. Mater.">65</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> corresponding to a specific energy of 323&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> (based on the total active mass of the cathode and anode).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0038_R_d5949537e1835" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Fuel Process. Technol.">38</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup> Moreover, a high rate capability of 180 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> maintained even at a current rate of 10 A g<sup>−1</sup> (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0005">5c</a>) at 25 °C, corresponding to the power density of 7.02&nbsp;kW kg<sup>−1</sup>. As well as a stable capacity of ≈206 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 2 A g<sup>−1</sup> over 650 cycles is delivered (86% capacity retention) (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0005">5d</a>) at 25 °C. The Zn-HC||NVP coin cell also tested at −40 °C and delivers a specific capacity of about 253 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> at 50&nbsp;mA g<sup>−1</sup> and specific energy of around 161&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> (Figures <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S32</a> and <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S33</a>, Supporting Information). Totally, the achieved performances demonstrate that the as-fabricated Zn-HC/NVP system possesses excellent kinetics and superior stability and can find extensive applications where both high power and wide temperature range are required (Figure&nbsp;<a href="#adma202211461-fig-0005">5e,f</a>; Table <a class="suppLink scrollableLink" href="#support-information-section">S15</a>, Supporting Information).<sup>[</sup><span><sup><a href="#adma202211461-bib-0010" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0010_R_d5949537e1876" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 10 - Adv. Mater.">10</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0038" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0038_R_d5949537e1876" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 38 - Fuel Process. Technol.">38</a>, <a href="#adma202211461-bib-0066" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0066_R_d5949537e1876" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 66 - Energy Environ. Sci.">66</a>-<a href="#adma202211461-bib-0075" class="bibLink tab-link" id="adma202211461-bib-0075_R_d5949537e1876" data-tab="pane-pcw-references" aria-label="Reference 75 - Nat. Commun.">75</a></sup></span><sup>]</sup></p>
            
            <section class="article-section__inline-figure">
               <figure class="figure" id="adma202211461-fig-0005"><a target="_blank" href="/cms/asset/4a27ef1d-352b-47ff-9ca5-58a6838fd90b/adma202211461-fig-0005-m.jpg"><picture>
                        <source srcset="/cms/asset/4a27ef1d-352b-47ff-9ca5-58a6838fd90b/adma202211461-fig-0005-m.jpg" media="(min-width: 1650px)"><img class="figure__image" src="/cms/asset/ed184a4f-7ac4-4e65-851f-76f0c799ebe9/adma202211461-fig-0005-m.png" data-lg-src="/cms/asset/4a27ef1d-352b-47ff-9ca5-58a6838fd90b/adma202211461-fig-0005-m.jpg" alt="Details are in the caption following the image" title="Details are in the caption following the image" loading="lazy"></picture></a><figcaption class="figure__caption">
                     <div class="figure__caption__header"><strong class="figure__title">Figure 5<span style="font-weight:normal"></span></strong><div class="figure-extra"><a href="#" class="open-figure-link">Open in figure viewer</a><a href="/action/downloadFigures?id=adma202211461-fig-0005&amp;partId=&amp;doi=10.1002%2Fadma.202211461" class="ppt-figure-link"><i aria-hidden="true" class="icon-Icon_Download"></i><span>PowerPoint</span></a></div>
                     </div>
                     <div class="figure__caption figure__caption-text">a) Schematic of sodium-ion full-cell with Zn-HC anode and NVP cathode. b) A photo shows that a Zn-HC||NVP full-cell can light up 52 LED bulbs. c) The GCD curves at various current densities. d) Cycling stability. e,f) Ragone plot and cycling stability of the Zn-HC electrode compared with previously reported high-energy, high-power cathodes.</div>
                  </figcaption>
               </figure>
            </section>
         </section>
         </section>
      <section class="article-section__content" id="adma202211461-sec-0080">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202211461-sec-0080-title">3 Conclusions</h2>
         
         <p>We have elaborately constructed the DAFR-derived hard carbon microspheres incorporated with ZnN<sub>4</sub> configurations via a typical two-step process. The as synthesized sample exhibits superior rate performance, reversible capacity (546 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> @ 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>, 140 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> @ 50 A g<sup>−1</sup>), LT capacity (443 mAh g<sup>−1</sup> @ 0.05 A g<sup>−1</sup>) and ICE (84%), simultaneously achieves a superior balance between the energy density (323&nbsp;Wh kg<sup>−1</sup>) and power density (7.02&nbsp;kW kg<sup>−1</sup>) in SIBs. More importantly, we provide a fundamental understanding on the charge-storage mechanism of HC electrode at varied temperatures. We decode that the local structure or SEI modulation on HC could significantly suppress the <i>R</i><sub>SEI</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>s</sub>, and contribute boosted RT performance, while the intrinsic Na<sup>+</sup> migration or desolvation ability of the electrolyte represents the rate determining step for the LT charge transfer kinetics. This study provides a novel strategy to regulate both the complicated interfacial electrochemistry and electrode chemistry of HC based material for high performance Na storage from RT to LT.</p>
         </section>
      <div class="article-section__content">
         
         <h2 class="article-section__title section__title section1" id="adma202211461-sec-0090-title"> Acknowledgements</h2>
